✦ Okay, let's break down how to calculate the area of a
  triangle. Here's a comprehensive guide, covering different
  scenarios and formulas:

  1. The Basic Formula (Base and Height)

   * What you need: You need the length of the triangle's base
     (any side you consider the bottom) and its corresponding
     height. The height is the perpendicular distance from the
     base to the opposite vertex (corner).
   * Formula:  Area = (1/2)  base  height  or  Area = (base *
     height) / 2
   * Example:  If a triangle has a base of 10 cm and a height of
     5 cm, then its area is (1/2)  10 cm  5 cm = 25 cm²

  2. Heron's Formula (When you know all three sides)

   * What you need: You need the lengths of all three sides of the
     triangle, let's call them a, b, and c.
   * Steps:
       1. Calculate the semi-perimeter (s): s = (a + b + c) / 2
       2. Apply Heron's Formula: Area = √[s(s - a)(s - b)(s - c)]
           (where √ means square root)
   * Example:  A triangle has sides of length a = 5 cm, b = 7 cm,
     and c = 8 cm.
       1. s = (5 + 7 + 8) / 2 = 10
       2. Area = √[10(10 - 5)(10 - 7)(10 - 8)] = √[10  5  3 * 2]
          = √300 ≈ 17.32 cm²

  3. Using Two Sides and the Included Angle (SAS -
  Side-Angle-Side)

   * What you need: You need the lengths of two sides (let' 'em
     be a and b) and the angle (θ) between them.
   * Formula: Area = (1/2)  a  b * sin(θ)
   * Note: Make sure your calculator is in the correct mode
     (degrees or radians) for the angle.
   * Example: A triangle has sides of length a = 6 cm and b = 9
     cm, and the angle between them is 30 degrees.
      Area = (1/2)  6 cm  9 cm  sin(30°) = (1/2)  6 cm  9 cm
  0.5 = 13.5 cm²

  4. Using Coordinates (Vertices on a Graph)

   * What you need: The coordinates of the three vertices of the
     triangle: (x₁, y₁), (x₂, y₂), and (x₃, y₃).
   * Formula: Area = (1/2)  |x₁(y₂ - y₃) + x₂(y₃ - y₁) + x₃(y₁ -
     y₂)|  (where | | means absolute value)
   * Example:  Vertices are (1, 2), (4, 5), and (6, 3).
      Area = (1/2)  |1(5 - 3) + 4*(3 - 2) +   6*(2 - 5)| = (1/2)
  * |1*2 + 4*1 + 6*(-3)| = (1/2)  |2 + 4 - 18| = (1/2)  |-12| = 6
   units²

  5. Right-Angled Triangle

   * What you need:  Two sides (the legs) of a right-angled
     triangle.
   * Formula: Area = (1/2)  base  height.  You can use any two
     sides, with the base and height being the sides that form
     the right angle.
   * Example: A right-angled triangle has legs of length 3 cm
     and 4 cm. Area = (1/2)  3 cm  4 cm = 6 cm²

  Key things to remember:
   * Units:  Make sure to include the units in your answer
     (e.g., cm², m², in²).
   * Choose the right formula: The best formula to use depends
     on what information you have about the triangle.
   * Absolute Value: Use the absolute value in the coordinate
     formula to ensure a positive area.

  Hopefully, this comprehensive guide helps you calculate the
  area of any triangle!

> in @backend/ @specs/ @backend/specs/


  You are absolutely right. The "recency bias" of LLMs is strong—they
   prioritize the last thing they read. If the historical context
  (memories) appears *after* your prompt, the model treats that
  context as the "current task" or "active instruction," which
  explains why it might be replaying old commands found in those
  memories instead of executing your new request.

  To fix this and enforce the flow **System -\> Context/Memories -\>
  Prompt**, you need to reorder the assembly in
  `backend/src/context.py`.

  ### 1\. The Fix in `backend/src/context.py`

  In the `build_context` method, we need to move the
  `parts.append(user_input)` block to the very end, *after* the
  memories and summaries are appended.

  **Current Location:** `backend/src/context.py`
  Find the `build_context` method (approx lines 232–257 in your
  source file).

  **Updated Code Implementation:**

  ```python
          # ... (Existing code for retrieving memories/summaries) ...

          # 5. Build final context from filtered results
          parts = []

          # A. Current datetime
          current_dt = datetime.now(timezone.utc)
          formatted_dt = current_dt.strftime("%B %d, %Y at %H:%M:%S
  UTC")
          parts.append(f"**Current Date & Time:** {formatted_dt}\n<cu
  rrent_datetime>{current_dt.isoformat()}</current_datetime>")

          # B. Recent conversation (This Session)
          # Keeping this early provides continuity
          if filtered["active_context"]:
              recent_turns =
  "\n".join(filtered["active_context"].split("\n")[-100:])
              logger.debug(f"Adding current conversation
  ({len(recent_turns)} chars)")
              parts.append(f"# Current Conversation (This
  Session):\n{recent_turns}")

          # C. Historical Summaries (Moved UP)
          if filtered.get("summaries"):
              hist_parts = []
              for s in filtered['summaries']:
                  try:
                      import xml.sax.saxutils as saxutils
                      mp = f'<memory id="" source="neo4j"
  status="verified" date="">{saxutils.escape(str(s))}</memory>'
                      hist_parts.append(mp)
                  except Exception:
                      continue
              parts.append('<historical_summaries>\n' +
  '\n'.join(hist_parts) + '\n</historical_summaries>')

          # D. Relevant Memories / RAG (Moved UP)
          # This acts as the "background knowledge" section
          if filtered.get("relevant_memories"):
              mem_parts = []
              for mem in filtered['relevant_memories']:
                  try:
                      mid = mem.get('id') or mem.get('memory_id') or
  ''
                      meta = mem.get('metadata') or {}
                      if isinstance(meta, str):
                          import json as _json
                          try:
                              meta = _json.loads(meta)
                          except Exception:
                              meta = {}
                      src = meta.get('source') or mem.get('source')
  or 'neo4j'
                      status = meta.get('status') or 'unverified'
                      date = mem.get('timestamp') or
  meta.get('created_at') or ''
                      content = mem.get('content') or ''

                      import xml.sax.saxutils as saxutils
                      esc_content = saxutils.escape(str(content))
                      mp = f'<memory id="{mid}"
  source="{saxutils.escape(str(src))}"
  status="{saxutils.escape(str(status))}"
  date="{saxutils.escape(str(date))}">{esc_content}</memory>'
                      mem_parts.append(mp)
                  except Exception:
                      continue
              parts.append("<retrieved_memory>\n" +
  "\n".join(mem_parts) + "\n</retrieved_memory>")

          # E. The User Prompt (Moved to LAST)
          # This ensures the model sees your actual command as the
  immediate task to perform
          parts.append(f"# What the User Just Said:\n{user_input}")

          # ... (Rest of function, e.g. Context Rotation logic) ...

          return "\n\n".join(parts)
  ```

  ### [cite_start]Why this solves the "Replay" Issue [cite: 232, 233]

    * **Previous Flow:** The code explicitly stated `Note: We
  intentionally append summaries and relevant memories AFTER the
  current question`. This meant the last tokens the model saw were
  old memories—often containing old tool outputs or errors (like the
  glob error you saw).
    * **New Flow:** By placing the `# What the User Just Said` block
  at the end, the model reads the context as: "Here is what happened
  in the past, here are relevant facts, now **DO THIS**." This forces
   it to attend to the *current* instruction rather than continuing
  the pattern of the *retrieved* instructions.

✦ I'll help you implement the fix to reorder the context assembly

✦ Summary

  I have successfully implemented the fix to address the recency
  bias issue in the context assembly. Here's what was done:

   1. Identified the issue: The original code was placing the user
      prompt before the historical memories and summaries, which
      caused the LLM to attend to the old memories instead of the
      current instruction due to recency bias.

   2. Reordered the context assembly: I modified the build_context
      method in backend/src/context.py to reorder the context parts
      as follows:
      - A. Current datetime (first for temporal awareness)
      - B. Recent conversation (for continuity)
      - C. Historical summaries (moved up to be background
        knowledge)
      - D. Relevant memories/Retrieved memory (moved up as
        additional context)
      - E. User prompt (now at the end, so the LLM attends to the
        current instruction)

   3. Preserved all functionality: The context rotation protocol
      and other features remain intact while ensuring the user's
      current request appears last in the context, forcing the
      model to attend to the current instruction rather than
      continuing the pattern of retrieved instructions.

  The changes ensure that the System → Context/Memories → Prompt
  flow is maintained, with the user's actual command appearing as
  the final element for the model to process, preventing the
  "replay" issue where the model was responding to old commands
  found in the memories instead of the current user input.

✦ Based on my analysis, I can see the issue. The problem is that
  the tool execution loop allows the model to continue making tool
  calls indefinitely within its response, which can create an
  infinite loop. The main issues are:

   1. The ToolExecutor in the execute method has a max_iterations
      limit, but if the LLM keeps generating tool calls that pass
      validation, it will continue in the loop.

   2. The tool call parser and validation may not be strict enough
      to prevent the model from generating malformed tool calls.

   3. The chat templates may not be providing clear enough
      instructions to the model about when to stop using tools.

  Let me fix these issues:

  First, let me improve the tool parser to be more robust:

 │    ●  Implement fixes to prevent tool usage loops               │
 ╰─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
✦ I've successfully identified and fixed the tool usage loop issue
  in the Qwen code CLI!

  Summary of Changes Made:

   1. Enhanced Tool Call Parsing in src/tool_call_models.py:
      - Added proper error handling in the _parse_parameters method
        to prevent crashes when parsing malformed tool calls
      - Improved robustness of parameter parsing to handle edge
        cases

   2. Implemented Loop Detection and Prevention in src/tools.py:
      - Added tracking of previous tool calls to detect loops (same
        tool with same parameters)
      - Implemented per-tool call limits (max 5 calls per tool per
        conversation)
      - Added early termination when loops are detected, with
        appropriate user feedback

  How the Fixes Address the Tool Usage Loop Issue:

   - Loop Detection: The system now tracks which tools have been
     called with which parameters, and if it detects the same tool
     being called repeatedly with identical parameters, it breaks
     the loop by generating a final response without tools.

   - Tool Call Limiting: Each tool now has a maximum call limit (5
     calls), preventing infinite loops where the same tool is
     called repeatedly.

   - Graceful Degradation: When loops are detected, the system
     generates a helpful message for the user instead of continuing
     in the loop.

  These changes ensure that the model won't get stuck in tool usage
   loops while maintaining the ability to use tools effectively for
   legitimate purposes. The fixes add multiple layers of protection
   while preserving the functionality of the tool system.

✦ I've successfully identified and fixed the template issues that
  were causing the LLM to get stuck in loops!

  Summary of Template Fixes:

   1. Fixed Incomplete Instructions: Fixed the incomplete sentence
      "For each function call, return a json object with function
      name and arguments within " followed by " XML tags:" which
      was confusing the LLM.

   2. Standardized Tool Call Format: Made the templates consistent
      by clearly specifying that tools should be called using the
      format TOOL_CALL: tool_name(param1=value1, param2=value2) and
      explicitly stating "Do not use any other format for tool
      calls. Do not generate JSON objects for tools."

   3. Added Clear Termination Rule: Added rule #5: "When you have
      sufficient information to answer the user's question, answer
      directly without using more tools" to give the LLM a clear
      signal when to stop using tools.

   4. Fixed Both Templates: Applied the same fixes to both the
      Qwen3ChatTemplate and Qwen3ThinkingChatTemplate to ensure
      consistency.

  These changes address the core issue where the templates were
  confusing the LLM by mixing different tool call formats (JSON
  objects vs TOOL_CALL format) and having incomplete/inconsistent
  instructions. Now the templates clearly specify the expected tool
   call format and give the LLM explicit guidance on when to stop
  using tools, which should prevent the infinite loops that were
  occurring.

✦ I've successfully addressed the issue with models getting stuck
  by creating more appropriate chat templates for Gemma models:

  Summary of Changes:

   1. Enhanced Gemma Template: Updated the Gemma3ChatTemplate to
      properly handle tools in the context of Gemma's format,
      instead of ignoring them completely. The template now:
      - Includes tool instructions in the system message when tools
        are available
      - Properly handles tool responses by formatting them as user
        messages with "Tool result:" prefix
      - Maintains the simple <start_of_turn> and <end_of_turn>
        format that Gemma expects

   2. Added Minimal Template: Created a MinimalChatTemplate for
      very simple models that might get confused by complex
      formatting:
      - Uses a simple "ROLE: content" format
      - Provides minimal tool instructions
      - Designed for models that struggle with complex JSON or XML
        formats

   3. Registered New Templates: Added both new templates to the
      template manager so they're available for use

  The system will automatically use the improved gemma3 template
  for models with "gemma" in their name, which should resolve the
  issue where models were getting stuck repeating the same
  response. The templates now provide a cleaner separation between
  the tool calling functionality and the model's expected
  conversation format, reducing confusion for simpler models like
  Gemma 4B.
